Geolabs provided earth observation and testing services for the mass grading and
fine grading of Makakilo C D Phase 2 Kahiwelo residential subdivision project in
Makakilo Oahu Hawaii In general our geotechnical engineering observation and testing
during the grading and backfilling operations were performed from to
The results of our field observations and compaction tests are provided
in the attached geotechnical engineering observations and testing services report for the
project dated
I certify that Geolabs performed the earthwork compaction tests To the best of
our knowledge it is our professional opinion that the site mass grading and fine grading
works observed by Geolabs has been performed in general conformance with the
approved plans and Standard Specifications for Public Works Construction City County
of Honolulu our geotechnical report and subsequent recommendations provided for the
above project

GEOTECHNICAL ENGINEERING OBSERVATIONS AND TESTING SERVICES
MAKAKILO C D PHASE 2 KAHIWELO
Dear Ms Yanagawa
This report summarizes our geotechnical engineering observations and testing
services performed during the grading and construction for Makakilo C D Phase 2
Kahiwelo project from to in accordance with our fee
proposal dated March 28 2011
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS
The Makakilo C D Phase 2 Kahiwelo is a residential subdivision development
project in Makakilo on the Island of Oahu Hawaii The project involved grading and
development of approximately 270 acres of property on the eastern side of Makakilo Drive
The project site is bordered by Interstate H 1 highway to the south Welo and Pueonani
Streets to the north Makakilo Gulch to the east and Makakilo Drive to the west as shown
on the Project Location Map Plate 1
The entire development was divided into three phases Phase 1 for the 180 single
family homes at the lower portion of the development parcels Phase 2 includes building
277 single family homes and townhouses at the upper northwest portion of the
development And Phase 3 located at the upper northeastern parcels of the development
is currently pending zoning application This report covers our grading observations and
testing services for the Phase 2 development
To achieve the design grades for the Phase 2 development site grading consisted
of excavations and embankments on the order of about 30 feet which were keyed and
benched into the existing ground during construction Our services during grading and
backfilling operation consisted of in situ moisture and density testing to determine
adequacy of compaction of embankment fills including backfills for infrastructure and utility
D R Horton Schuler Division
Page 2
W O 5407 30 Rev
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
installations compaction testing for building pads garages walkways and driveways This
report summarizes our field observations and compaction testing services during site
grading operations for the project
SITE GRADING
Delta Construction Corporation performed the earthwork operations for the project
At the on set of earthwork areas within the contract grading limits were generally cleared
and grubbed of vegetation and deleterious materials Materials generated from the clearing
operations were disposed of off site Following the clearing and grubbing operations the
areas to be cut were excavated Finish grades were compacted using a sheepsfoot and or
smooth drum vibratory roller
In general on site excess soil materials generated from the excavation were primarily
used in the trench backfill and some fill slopes The on site fill materials generally consisted
of silty and clayey soils with some gravel In addition on site rock materials generated from
the excavation were crushed to 3 inch minus meeting selected granular fill requirements
The expansion of the on site fill material ranged from low to high Samples of the fill
and backfill materials utilized during construction were obtained and transported to our office
for laboratory testing The maximum dry densities and optimum moisture contents were
established in our laboratory in general accordance with ASTM D1557 Modified Proctor
The test results are summarized on Plates 4 1 and 4 2 of this report
In general fill materials consist of low expansive 3 inch minus materials placed for
the fills and utility trench backfills while 12 inch minus general fills were placed about 5 feet
below finished subgrade Field density tests were performed in general accordance with
ASTM D6938 Nuclear Gauge Method where appropriate During the fill and backfill
operations the materials were generally placed in near level lifts brought to near the
optimum moisture and compacted to obtain the specified degree of compaction based on
visual observations and or field density tests Periodic field density tests were performed
during the fill and backfill operations to confirm our field observations as variations in
construction procedures and soil conditions were noted
Over excavation of about 2 to 3 feet was conducted at the lots where expansive
soil was encountered at the subgrade of the house foundation On site or imported low
expansive soils were used to backfill the over excavation
Some of the lots were partially cut and partially filled The shallow fill and cut portions
of the lots were over excavated to 2 feet below finished grade and re compacted In
general the fills were compacted to at least 90 percent relative compaction where the
thickness of the fills was less than 15 feet Where the thickness of the fills was greater
than 15 feet the upper 15 feet of the fills were compacted to at least 90 percent relative
compaction and the remaining fills were compacted to at least 95 percent relative
compaction
D R Horton Schuler Division
Page 3
W O 5407 30 Rev
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
Slopes that received embankment fills were provided with keyways about 12 feet
wide and 2 feet deep at the toe and benched along the upper slopes
A total of 3 515 field density tests including re tests of failed areas were performed
in general accordance with ASTM D6938 Nuclear Gauge Method The results of the
compaction tests performed during construction of the above project are summarized on
Plates 3 1 through 3 222 of this report Test locations and elevations were estimated by
pacing and interpolating from on site survey stakes where available These locations and
elevations should be considered accurate only to the degree implied by the methods used
Based on the observations of our field representatives and the results of the
referenced tests it is our professional opinion that the earthwork operations for the Makakilo
C and D Phase 2 Kahiwelo subdivision project observed and tested by Geolabs in the
period covered by this report were performed in general conformance with the intent of the
plans and specifications and our recommendations in the following references
1
Chapter 14 of the Revised Ordinances of Honolulu 1990 as amended
2
Standard Specifications for Public Works Construction September 1986 City
and County of Honolulu
3
Report by Geolabs Inc entitled Geotechnical Engineering Exploration
Residential Development in Makakilo 72 73 and 81
Por Makakilo Oahu Hawaii dated
ADDITIONAL RECOMMENDATIONS FOR HOMEOWNER
Homeowners should immediately verify whether their swales have been
compromised or altered from the original condition of initial move in If these swales have
been altered consult your plot plan and reinstall the swales Swales should also be grassed
as leaving them bare will result in soil erosion during heavy rains
If the swales cannot be completely reinstalled because of constructed wall
obstructions installation of drain pipe along the rear and sides of the property can help
drain excess water away from the sidewalks and building slabs
If a homeowner constructs improvements or expansions beyond the original floor
area for example expanding the lanai adding another 1st floor bedroom or family room
etc the services of a qualified geotechnical engineer should be retained to evaluate the
soil conditions at their respective lot for site specific building recommendations
Excessive landscape watering within 3 feet of the foundations and slabs should be
avoided Gravel strips adjacent to slabs and foundations should be avoided Planters
next to foundations should be avoided or have concrete bottoms and drains to reduce
water infiltration into the subsoils
D R Horton Schuler Division
Page 4
W O 5407 30 Rev
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
LIMITATIONS
Geolabs assumes no responsibility for alterations made to finished grades on the
project subsequent to our observation and testing period without our knowledge and written
acknowledgment Lot owners should be advised not to block the surface drainage and to
obtain professional consultation in the planning design and construction of any future
improvements Lot owners should also be advised not to water excessively adjacent to the
house structure
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities
occurring simultaneously on a construction site therefore some work may have occurred
without our observation However we believe the level of earthwork observation and
testing services provided is reasonable in reducing the geotechnical risks to the project
It should be recognized that there are variations in the accuracy and statistical
repeatability of the tests and methods used to monitor the earthwork construction and
materials Our services were performed in accordance with generally accepted standards
of geotechnical engineering practice no warranty is expressed or implied Provision of
construction monitoring by an engineer is not insurance nor does it guarantee
construction of any type The contractor shall retain responsibility for the quality of the
work for adhering to the plans and specifications and for repairing defects regardless of
when they are found
D R Horton Schuler Division Page 5
W O 5407 30 Rev

We appreciate the opportunity to be of continued service to you on this project If
you have questions or need additional information please contact our office
Respectfully submitted
